          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Profiling Every GM Ahead of the 2015 NFL Draft" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/418/hi-res-48e408385b22feedc83fcc894a28317f_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Steve Dykes/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
             <span itemprop="caption">
              Jerry Jones was named 2014 NFL Executive of the Year by the Pro Football Writers Association.
             </span>
            </div>
           </div>

          <div class="article_info team-color-border cf">
           <div class="total-reads article-stats">
            <div class="team-color-text article-stats_count">
             196.0K
            </div>
            <div class="article-stats_label">
             Reads
            </div>
           </div>
           <div class="article_comments js-open-comments article-stats ">
            <div class="comments-count team-color-text article-stats_count">
             311
            </div>
            <div class="comments-label article-stats_label">
             Comments
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            In a little over a month, millions of amateur general managers, player personnel directors and scouts will spend three days analyzing and agonizing over the picks made by the 32 teams in the 2015
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/nfl" target="_blank">
             NFL
            </a>
            draft.
           </p>
           <p>
            Of course, thats their problem.
           </p>
           <p>
            What about the men who actually have to make the selection for their respective franchises? Theres an art to doing what these talent evaluators do, and like any profession, some are masters at their craft and others are still learning the ropes.
           </p>
           <p>
            So we present a bit of a thumbnail sketch for each of the 32 general managers in the
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/nfl">
             NFL
            </a>
            . In some cases, they dont even own the official title, but you will get the picture, as every franchise is run differently.
           </p>
           <p>
            We will look at these mens backgrounds in the league as well as their current clubs win-loss record under their guidance. We will also give you a little taste of these gentlemens biggest success stories as well as some of their failures when it comes to picking players, at least in our opinion. The main focus here will be on that mans work with the current franchise, with a few exceptions.
           </p>
           <p>
            Well follow all that up with a look at some trends and/or a little history when it comes to either the general manager or the team.
           </p>
           <p>
            We hope you enjoy this brief peek behind the curtain with the draft less than 40 days away.
           </p>
          </div>
          <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--next" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Begin Slideshow">
           Begin Slideshow
           <span class="aquo">
            
           </span>
          </a>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Arizona Cardinals: Steve Keim
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Arizona Cardinals: Steve Keim" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/419/hi-res-ef8ef58d84e00a10c3d93b547fc2134d_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Matt York/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Steve Keim, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Arizona Cardinals
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Keim joined the Cardinals organization in May of 1999 as a college scout and worked his way up the ranks. He was promoted to general manager on Jan. 8, 2013, and has overseen the teams last two drafts.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            21-11
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            S Tyrann Mathieu, RB Andre Ellington, WR John Brown
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Huge Swing and Miss:
            </strong>
            G Jonathan Cooper
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In two years at the helm, Keim has drafted 16 players, with 10 of those picks on the offensive side of the ball. Given the Cardinals free-agent haul this offseason on defense, look for Keim to lean offense once again this spring.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-3 cf display-none " data-page="3">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Atlanta Falcons: Thomas Dimitroff
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Atlanta Falcons: Thomas Dimitroff" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/420/hi-res-4e056b727bfae3d86bd7f6890f825d7e_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Scott Cunningham/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Thomas Dimitroff, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Atlanta Falcons
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Dimitroffs previous stops in the league include stints with the Detroit Lions and Cleveland Browns. He served as Director of College Scouting for the New England Patriots for five years (2003-07) before being hired by the Falcons in 2008.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            66-46
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/matt-ryan">
             Matt Ryan
            </a>
            , WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/julio-jones">
             Julio Jones
            </a>
            , S William Moore
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DT Peria Jerry, C Peter Konz
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Dimitroff has selected seven players in the first round since 2008, and the only position hes doubled up on is tackle (Sam Baker in 2008, Jake Matthews in 2014). In any case, new head coach Dan Quinn will have his input here in a big way, as
            <a href="http://espn.go.com/nfl/story/_/id/12272940/atlanta-falcons-owner-arthur-blank-says-new-coach-dan-quinn-final-say-53-man-roster" target="_blank">
             Vaughn McClure of ESPN.com
            </a>
            explained last month.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-4 cf display-none " data-page="4">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Baltimore Ravens: Ozzie Newsome
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Baltimore Ravens: Ozzie Newsome" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/422/hi-res-c769a34f2fd085a633d8fe0880109573_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Patrick Semansky/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ozzie Newsome, General Manager and Executive VP
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Baltimore Ravens
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Newsome is a Pro Football Hall of Fame tight end, and some would say he deserves that honor as an executive as well. Following his playing days with the Cleveland Browns, he would be a part of
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/bill-belichick">
             Bill Belichick
            </a>
            s staff and front office with the team. When the franchise relocated to Baltimore and became the Ravens in 1996, Newsome was named vice president of player personnel and the rest is historywhich includes a pair of Super Bowl titles.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            168-135-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            T Jonathan Ogden, LB Ray Lewis, OLB Peter Boulware, RB Jamal Lewis, TE Todd Heap, S Ed Reed, OLB Terrell Suggs, T Marshal Yanda, QB Joe Flacco
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            WR Pat Johnson, QB Chris Redman, QB Kyle Boller, DT Terrence Cody
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            The Ravens have drafted only three players in the first round over the last five years, and all have been on the defensive side of the ball. Its also worth mentioning that Newsome has selected a total of 19 players in the first round dating back to 1996, and 11 of those performers have been named to at least one Pro Bowl, including inside linebacker C.J. Mosley in 2014.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-5 cf display-none " data-page="5">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Buffalo Bills: Doug Whaley
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Buffalo Bills: Doug Whaley" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/932/135/hi-res-adddd31d521b2df8e971b48aa7016404_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Gary Wiepert/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Doug Whaley, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Buffalo Bills
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Whaley cut his teeth early with the Pittsburgh Steelers and spent 11 seasons as the franchises pro scouting coordinator. In 2010, he was named the Bills assistant general manager before being elevated to the top spot in 2013.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            15-17
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            LB Kiko Alonso, WR Robert Woods, WR Sammy Watkins, LB Preston Brown
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Swing and Miss:
            </strong>
            QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/ej-manuel">
             EJ Manuel
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Of course, it is indeed far too early to call Manuel a total miss, but it is also safe to say he has not progressed as expected two years into his career. Whaley has shown hes not afraid to move up and down in the first round, and the Bills dont have a Day 1 pick on April 30 after trading up to the No. 4 spot last year to draft Watkins.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Carolina Panthers: Dave Gettleman
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Carolina Panthers: Dave Gettleman" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/423/hi-res-0615e2485f3e98f0f9a8acfd1d7cf230_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Chuck Burton/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Dave Gettleman, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Carolina Panthers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            A veteran of NFL front offices for nearly 30 years, Gettleman worked for the Buffalo Bills, Denver Broncos and New York Giants prior to taking the Panthers GM job in 2013.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            19-12-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            DT Star Lotulelei, DT Kawann Short, WR Kelvin Benjamin
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Under Gettleman, the Panthers have been big players in the draft so far. Carolina has made just 11 selections the past two seasons, but many have panned out. His two first-round picks to date, Lotulelei and Benjamin, have played very well, while Short was one of the better defensive tackles in the league this past season.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Chicago Bears: Ryan Pace
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Chicago Bears: Ryan Pace" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/424/hi-res-5fce1d7c7babfc62f9560e9db0c77de0_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Nam Y. Huh/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ryan Pace, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Chicago Bears
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Prior to his arrival in the Windy City, Pace spent 14 years with the New Orleans Saints13 of those in the player personnel department working under general manager Mickey Loomis.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            First season with Bears
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Last year, it was general manager Phil Emery that used the teams first three picks and four of its five selections on the defensive side of the football. Pace has already added his share of free agents on defense, but in his first draft running the show, will he employ the same strategy as Emery did a year ago?
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Cincinnati Bengals: Marvin Lewis, Duke Tobin
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Cincinnati Bengals: Marvin Lewis, Duke Tobin" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/425/hi-res-72fb1ecaa4c3e4c6f15e49a2863cf86b_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Al Behrman/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Duke Tobin, Director of Player Personnel
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Cincinnati Bengals
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            The Bengals dont really have an official general manager, as Tobin, head coach Marvin Lewis, team president Paul Brownas well as otherseach have a say. But as
            <a href="http://www.nfl.com/news/story/0ap2000000367536/article/mike-brown-ceding-bengals-control-to-marvin-lewis" target="_blank">
             Chris Wesseling of NFL.com
            </a>
            explained last July (and reiterated by others), Brown has taken a back seat since 2010 (his brother, Pete, is the teams senior vice president of player personnel). These days, it has been much more about Tobin and Lewis dating back to the last five drafts (and we will use that as a jumping-off point).
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            44-35 since 2010
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            DT Geno Atkins, WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/aj-green">
             A.J. Green
            </a>
            , QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/andy-dalton">
             Andy Dalton
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            The Bengals traditionally stand pat with the picks they get and are not very active when it comes to trades. That philosophy has served them quite well in recent years, and it has resulted in strong draft classes and a franchise-record four consecutive playoff appearancesand counting.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-9 cf display-none " data-page="9">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Cleveland Browns: Ray Farmer
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Cleveland Browns: Ray Farmer" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/426/hi-res-754e3a0dd11745bd736edf1ab6428040_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jason Miller/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ray Farmer, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Cleveland Browns
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Prior to becoming the Browns general manager one year ago, Farmer spent seven seasons with the Kansas City Chiefs as their pro personnel director. Prior to that, he was with the Atlanta Falcons for four years as a scout under the guidance of Les Snead and Rich McKay.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            7-9
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            G Joel Bitonio, RB Terrance West
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            We will get a better idea of Farmer's trends after this year, especially with the Browns having 10 picks as of nowincluding Nos. 12 and 19 overall. A year ago, he moved up and down in the first round and would settle on cornerback Justin Gilbert and quarterback
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/johnny-manziel">
             Johnny Manziel
            </a>
            , neither of who did much to distinguish themselves on the field.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-10 cf display-none " data-page="10">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Dallas Cowboys: Jerry Jones
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Dallas Cowboys: Jerry Jones" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/431/hi-res-9c1f738f777681849ad83ce7b51ad9fe_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Rob Carr/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Jerry Jones, Owner/President/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Dallas Cowboys
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Jones purchased the Cowboys in 1989 and has been the centerpiece of the organization ever since. While hes been far from a one-man show over the years (see head coach Jimmy Johnsons magical touch from 1989-93 as well as Bill Parcells handiwork from 2003-06), he has the title of general manager and it is one of many hats he has worn since purchasing the franchise.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            226-190
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB Troy Aikman, RB Emmitt Smith, G Larry Allen, TE Jason Witten, DE DeMarcus Ware
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DE Shante Carver, TE David LaFleur, LB Bobby Carpenter
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Talk about a grand slam. Since 2010, the Cowboys have drafted five players in the first round and four of them (wide receiver
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/dez-bryant">
             Dez Bryant
            </a>
            , tackle Tyron Smith, center Travis Frederick and guard Zack Martin) have been named to at least one Pro Bowl. Before grabbing Smith in 2010, Dallas had not used a first-round pick on an offensive lineman since 1981.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-11 cf display-none " data-page="11">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Denver Broncos: John Elway
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Denver Broncos: John Elway" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/432/hi-res-a8ee1456983f7d48bf13b18056eccf85_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Justin Edmonds/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            John Elway, Executive VP of Football Operations/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Denver Broncos
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            The Pro Football Hall of Famer and two-time Super Bowl champion signal-caller is now calling the shots for the team he played 16 seasons for. Elway became the leader of the franchise in 2011 and has had the team in the playoffs each of his first four years on the job.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            46-18
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            LB Von Miller, TE Julius Thomas, G/T Orlando Franklin
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Elway has had three first-round picks since taking over in 2011, and all have been used on defense. The last offensive players the team drafted in the first round were wide receiver
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/demaryius-thomas">
             Demaryius Thomas
            </a>
            (22nd overall) and quarterback
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/tim-tebow">
             Tim Tebow
            </a>
            (25th overall) in 2010.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Detroit Lions: Martin Mayhew
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Detroit Lions: Martin Mayhew" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/427/hi-res-5223ff431fe25e55adf93e11d25b5133_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Paul Sancya/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Martin Mayhew, Executive VP of Football Operations/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Detroit Lions
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Many remember Mayhew during his playing days with the Buffalo Bills, Washington Redskins and Tampa Bay Buccaneers.
           </p>
           <p>
            Now he begins his 15th season in the Lions front office. Martin has been the teams top executive since September of 2008, when he replaced then-general manager Matt Millen three games into a season that would end with an 0-16 record (
            <em>
             Note
            </em>
            :The teams listed win-loss record under Mayhew begins with the 2009 season.)
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            40-56
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/matthew-stafford">
             Matthew Stafford
            </a>
            , LB DeAndre Levy, DT Ndamukong Suh
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            WR Titus Young, WR Ryan Broyles
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Mayhew has done a good job adding talent through the draft, and it will be interesting to see how recent first-round picks such as defensive end Ziggy Ansah and tight end Eric Ebron progress.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Green Bay Packers: Ted Thompson
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Green Bay Packers: Ted Thompson" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/428/hi-res-c9d1a2d8a74b8ad70d84a07392e90fc0_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              David J. Phillip/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ted Thompson, Executive VP/General Manager/Director of Football Operations
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Green Bay Packers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Where to begin? When it comes to talent evaluating, this is Thompsons second tour of duty with the Packers, as he's held various titles in player personnel from 1992-99. After spending five seasons as the Seattle Seahawks vice president of football operations, Thompson returned to Green Bay as the teams general manager, succeeding Mike Sherman (2001-05).
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            98-61-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/aaron-rodgers">
             Aaron Rodgers
            </a>
            , WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/greg-jennings">
             Greg Jennings
            </a>
            , WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/jordy-nelson">
             Jordy Nelson
            </a>
            , LB Clay Matthews, WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/randall-cobb">
             Randall Cobb
            </a>
            , RB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/eddie-lacy">
             Eddie Lacy
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DT Justin Harrell, QB Brian Brohm, CB Patrick Lee, DE Jerel Worthy
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Thompson and the Packers rely almost solely on the draft to maintain their roster. When the Green Bay defense fell on hard times in 2011, he used his first six picks in 2012 on defense. A year later, four of his five selections were on the offensive side of the ball.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Houston Texans: Rick Smith
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Houston Texans: Rick Smith" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/429/hi-res-86ba441bb3976aa0f1a0620c6f344ad4_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Phelan M. Ebenhack/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Rick Smith, General Manager/Executive VP of Football Operations
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Houston Texans
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Smith was named general manager of the Texans in June of 2006 shortly after Charley Casserly stepped down from the post roughly six weeks after orchestrating the teams draft that year (which included the likes of Mario Williams, DeMeco Ryans, Eric Winston and Owen Daniels).
           </p>
           <p>
            Prior to his arrival in Houston, Smith worked in the pro personnel department with the Denver Broncos, which he joined after his playing career with the franchise.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            70-74
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            WR/KR Jacoby Jones, T Duane Brown, LB Brian Cushing, DE J.J. Watt
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DT Amobi Okoye, CB Brandon Harris
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Smith has chosen eight players in the first round dating back to 2007, and six of those have been on defense. Thats nothing new for this franchise, even before Smiths arrival. The Texans have used 12 of their last 14 first-round picks on the defensive side of the ballthis after selecting quarterback David Carr (2002) and wide receiver
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/andre-johnson">
             Andre Johnson
            </a>
            (2003) the first two years, respectively.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-15 cf display-none " data-page="15">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>

             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">
              15
              <span class="br-light-grey">
               of
              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Indianapolis Colts: Ryan Grigson
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Indianapolis Colts: Ryan Grigson" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/430/hi-res-9450cd46538c4420dfce5b39593e3f3e_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Michael Conroy/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ryan Grigson, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Indianapolis Colts
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            A sixth-round draft choice by the Cincinnati Bengals in 1995, Grigsons playing career in both the NFL and later theCFLnever amounted to much. A scout with the St. Louis Rams in 1999, he would join the Philadelphia Eagles as a regional scout in 2004. By 2010, he was the teams director of player personnel before being named the Colts general manager in 2012.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            33-15
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/andrew-luck">
             Andrew Luck
            </a>
            , WR T.Y. Hilton, TE Dwayne Allen, TE Coby Fleener
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In three years of leading the Colts, Grigson has drafted 22 players, with two-thirds of those selections (15) coming on the offensive side of the ball. Last May, he only had five picks at his disposal.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Jacksonville Jaguars: David Caldwell
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Jacksonville Jaguars: David Caldwell" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/433/hi-res-a0bb230ff66d652f2811174ae1a28f5e_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Scott Halleran/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            David Caldwell, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Jacksonville Jaguars
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Caldwells background prior to joining the Jaguars in 2013 saw him spend time with the Carolina Panthers, Indianapolis Colts and Atlanta Falcons. The five seasons before taking over in Jacksonville, he was the Falcons director of college scouting (2008-11) and director of player personnel (2012) under general manager Thomas Dimitroff.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            7-25
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            No big hits yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In his first draft with the team in 2013, Caldwell used five of his eight selections on defensive backs. A year ago, he used his first four picks to bolster the offense, grabbing quarterback Blake Bortles with the third overall pick and a pair of wide receivers (Marqise Lee and Allen Robinson) in the second round.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Kansas City Chiefs: John Dorsey
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Kansas City Chiefs: John Dorsey" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/932/210/hi-res-0aefde3fe83e6b793a9fbdb792008169_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Charlie Riedel/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            John Dorsey, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Kansas City Chiefs
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            First hired by Pro Football Hall of Fame executive Ron Wolf in Green Bay, Dorsey was hired to be the Packers director of college scouting for 12 years (2000-11) and then the teams director of football operations in 2012 before heading to Kansas City in 2013.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            20-12
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            TE Travis Kelce
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Dorsey has drafted 14 players in two years, and nine of those players have come on offense. He used his first three selections in 2013 and last four picks in 2014 on that side of the ball. Its also worth noting that due to trades, the Chiefs have not had a second-round draft choice the last two years.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Minnesota Vikings: Rick Spielman
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Minnesota Vikings: Rick Spielman" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/932/212/hi-res-af733cda7858c14435be888744849383_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Hannah Foslien/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Rick Spielman, Executive VP and General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Minnesota Vikings
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            While hes
            <span>
             only
            </span>
            had the title of general manager since 2012, Spielman has been with the organization since May of 2006 and has been in the business of directing their drafts since 2007 (which is what the win-loss record below will reflect). Prior to his arrival in the Twin Cities, his work in NFL front offices included tenures with the Detroit Lions, Chicago Bears and Miami Dolphins.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            61-66-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            RB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/adrian-peterson">
             Adrian Peterson
            </a>
            , TE Kyle Rudolph, T Matt Kalil, S Harrison Smith
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            S Tyrell Johnson, QB Christian Ponder
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Spielman has been busy in the first round as of late, selecting seven players on Day 1 since 2012 and at least two players each of the last three years.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New England Patriots: Bill Belichick (Head Coach)
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="New England Patriots: Bill Belichick (Head Coach)" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/932/213/hi-res-a0302de8a21536869455695d07aaa4a4_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              David J. Phillip/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Bill Belichick, Head Coach
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            New England Patriots
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            We all know he runs the show in Foxborough and that his NFL lineage dates back to 1975 as a special assistant with the Baltimore Colts. Belichick was also an assistant with the Detroit Lions, Denver Broncos and New York Giants. In 1991, he was named head coach of the Cleveland Browns and was building something there before the franchise moved to Baltimore. His first stint with the Patriots came in 1996, and one year later, he followed Bill Parcells to the New York Jets. Hes been at the controls of the New England Patriots since 2000.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as Head Coach:
            </strong>
            175-65
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            QB Tom Brady, DT Richard Seymour, DT Vince Wilfork, G Logan Mankins, DB Devin McCourty, TE
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/rob-gronkowski">
             Rob Gronkowski
            </a>
            , WR Julian Edelman
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            T Adrian Klemm, QB Rohan Davey, WR Chad Jackson, CB Terrence Wheatley
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In late January,
            <a href="http://grantland.com/the-triangle/bill-belichick-nfl-draft-new-england-patriots/" target="_blank">
             Bill Barnwell of Grantland.com
            </a>
            outlined Belichicks history in the NFL draft. For years, he would trade for future picks, but as of late, hes been using them and, as usual, is coming up with good players. Belichick has had his problems finding wide receivers in the draft, so nobodys perfect.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New Orleans Saints: Mickey Loomis
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="New Orleans Saints: Mickey Loomis" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/932/214/hi-res-5c3fe3e7ace2947ee6aee982fad7a886_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Bill Haber/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Mickey Loomis, Executive VP/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            New Orleans Saints
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Loomis has been with the Saints since 2000, but at his current position since 2002. Prior to coming to New Orleans, he spent 15 years with the Seattle Seahawks and was the teams executive vice president from 1992-98.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            115-93
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            C LeCharles Bentley, G Jahri Evans, WR Marques Colston, TE
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/jimmy-graham">
             Jimmy Graham
            </a>
            , DE Cameron Jordan, DT Akiem Hicks, S Kenny Vaccaro
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DT Johnathan Sullivan, DT Sedrick Ellis, T Charles Brown
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Due to trades and other issues, the Saints havent drafted at least seven players in one year since 2007. However, its also worth noting that due to the Graham trade to Seattle, the team will have a pair of first-round draft choices in April.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New York Giants: Jerry Reese
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="New York Giants: Jerry Reese" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/434/hi-res-328187ab36b3971d5c64962792286a64_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Seth Wenig/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Jerry Reese, Senior VP/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            New York Giants
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            A member of the organization since 1994, Reese took over for general managerErnie Accorsiin 2007 and has been at the helm of a franchise that has won two Super Bowls. He was a member of the Giants scouting department in 1994 and would eventually become the teams director of player personnel in 2002.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            71-57
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            CB Terrell Thomas, DE Jason Pierre-Paul, WR Odell Beckham Jr.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            S Kenny Phillips, LB Clint Sintim, DT Marvin Austin
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Reese has shown an ability to find good players not only in the draft, but with undrafted performers such as wideout
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/victor-cruz">
             Victor Cruz
            </a>
            and tight end Jake Ballard. The Giants have gone offense in the first round three consecutive years.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             New York Jets: Mike Maccagnan
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="New York Jets: Mike Maccagnan" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/435/hi-res-f4258d52cec71104b94fecc944093156_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Julio Cortez/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Mike Maccagnan, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            New York Jets
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Talk about being all over the world? Maccagnan has worked for the World League of American Football and enjoyed stints with Saskatchewan and Ottawa of the CFL. He spent seven seasons with the Washington Redskins as a college and pro scout before moving onto the Houston Texans, where he was a member of the college scouting department for 15 years.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            First season with Jets
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Having apparently solved their cornerback issues with the free-agent additions of Darrelle Revis, Antonio Cromartie and Buster Skrine, will Maccagnan and head coach Todd Bowles go after a quarterback with the sixth overall pick? The franchise hasnt used a first-round selection on an offensive player since grabbing quarterback
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/mark-sanchez">
             Mark Sanchez
            </a>
            in 2009.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-24 cf display-none " data-page="24">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Oakland Raiders: Reggie McKenzie
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Oakland Raiders: Reggie McKenzie" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/436/hi-res-32250a9858a1d81cf9e98c8e3cb48813_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Ben Margot/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Reggie McKenzie, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Oakland Raiders
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            The past three seasons, McKenzie has been the talent evaluator and selector for the Silver and Black. He spent the previous 18 years in the personnel department of the Green Bay Packers.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            11-37
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            LB Sio Moore, LB Khalil Mack, QB Derek Carr
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            G Tony Bergstrom, T Menelik Watson
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In his first year at the helm, McKenzie was without early-round picks due to the trade for quarterback Carson Palmer and the supplemental draft (quarterback
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/terrelle-pryor">
             Terrelle Pryor
            </a>
            ). He made six selections in 2012, and three were compensatory picks which could not be dealt. Last year, he scored with Mack and Carr, and we will now start to get an idea of his method of operation.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Philadelphia Eagles: Chip Kelly (Head Coach)
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Philadelphia Eagles: Chip Kelly (Head Coach)" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/437/hi-res-ef5543529bd64791f2aa8df4fa202e41_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Paul Sancya/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Chip Kelly, Head Coach
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Philadelphia Eagles
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            This will be first year that Kelly will be in total charge of the draft.
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/articles/2318439-insider-buzz-increased-draft-power-will-test-chip-kellys-eagles-and-nfl-future" target="_blank">
             Bleacher Report colleague Jason Cole
            </a>
            has the skinny on the issue between him and Howie Roseman the last two years.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as Head Coach:
            </strong>
            20-12
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            No big hits yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Other than optioning for any player from the University of Oregon, which he has done via trades and free agency this offseason, theres no real track record when it comes to Kellys draft touch.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Pittsburgh Steelers: Kevin Colbert
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Pittsburgh Steelers: Kevin Colbert" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/438/hi-res-63d50e1705c964898982cd043afd602d_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              David J. Phillip/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Kevin Colbert, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Pittsburgh Steelers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            From the Miami Dolphins in the late 1980s to becoming the Detroit Lions pro scouting director in 1990 (a job he had for 10 years), Colbert has been at this for quite some time and his impressive track record bears that out. He begins his 16th year in the Steel City, and be it as director of football operations (2000-10) or finally under the official title of general manager (since 2011), hes handled the draft for the franchise since the start of the century.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            154-85-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            SS
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/troy-polamalu">
             Troy Polamalu
            </a>
            , QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/ben-roethlisberger">
             Ben Roethlisberger
            </a>
            , C Maurkice Pouncey, WR
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/antonio-brown">
             Antonio Brown
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            DE Alonzo Jackson, DE Ziggy Hood, WR Limas Sweed, LB Bruce Davis, T Mike Adams
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            You can usually find the Steelers in the bottom half or third of each round, and Colbert more times than not has done well in the first round. Where hes had his bad luck at times is the second round, although theres nothing bad to be said about his pick in 2013 of running back LeVeon Bell. Like Green Bay, the Steelers are draft dependent and their track record has been solid.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-27 cf display-none " data-page="27">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             St. Louis Rams: Les Snead
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="St. Louis Rams: Les Snead" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/439/hi-res-14dc334b04ebb489e4e064127de5c62f_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Jeff Roberson/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Les Snead, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            St. Louis Rams
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Snead was named the Rams general manager in 2012. Prior to his arrival in the Gateway City, he spent 13 seasons with the Atlanta Falcons personnel department. Snead was also part of the Jacksonville Jaguars original front office from 1995-97.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            20-27-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            DT Michael Brockers, LB Alec Ogletree, DT Aaron Donald
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            RB Isaiah Pead
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Like Rick Spielman in Minnesota, Snead has been quite busy when it comes to the first round. In 2012, he orchestrated the trade with the Washington Redskins that netted them additional Day 1 picks in 2013 and 2014. The Rams have taken five players in the first round the last three years. They own the 10th overall pick this year, and dont be surprised if Snead is on the move again.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             San Diego Chargers: Tom Telesco
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="San Diego Chargers: Tom Telesco" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/440/hi-res-d0154ce45f59d1ea055cf9d81b559e98_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Phelan M. Ebenhack/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Tom Telesco, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            San Diego Chargers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Before taking over in San Diego in 2013, Telesco spent 15 years in the front office of the Indianapolis Colts and was the teams vice president of football operations. Once a training camp intern with the Buffalo Billsmost of that under the guidance of Bill PolianTelesco would later follow the Pro Football Hall of Fame executive to Carolina before both men made their way to Indianapolis.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            18-14
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            T D.J. Fluker, WR Keenan Allen
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Not a lot to go on due to the small track record. For what its worth, Telesco has drafted six players each of the last two years, and in each instance, hasnt doubled up on any one position.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            </h2>
