          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="San Francisco 49ers: Trent Baalke" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/441/hi-res-4edbe991de879780bf78d22e42d62f79_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>

          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Trent Baalke, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            San Francisco 49ers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            A former collegiate assistant coach, Baalkes NFL career began as a scout with the New York Jets (1998-2000). He later made his way to Washington and was part of the Redskins scouting department. He would be hired by the San Francisco 49ers in 2005, and three years later, was named the franchises director of player personnel. Hes been calling the shots on the NFL draft since 2010 after Scot McCloughan left the team.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            50-29-1
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            G Mike Iupati, LB NaVorro Bowman, LB Aldon Smith, QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/colin-kaepernick">
             Colin Kaepernick
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            S Taylor Mays, WR A.J. Jenkins
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Baalke has had his share of hits and misses since 2008. One position he seems to covet drafting is running back, but hes never selected one in the first round.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Seattle Seahawks: John Schneider
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Seattle Seahawks: John Schneider" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/442/hi-res-d15a7c0ae3344da524c5f3a0dc7c7ddc_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Elaine Thompson/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            John Schneider, Executive VP/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Seattle Seahawks
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Schneider began his NFL front-office career as an intern under then-Green Bay Packers executive Ron Wolf. His travels would eventually take him to Kansas City, Seattle and Washington before he returned to Titletown. He returned to the Seahawks in 2010 as the teams general manager.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            50-30
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            FS Earl Thomas, WR Golden Tate, SS Kam Chancellor, CB Richard Sherman, LB Bobby Wagner, QB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/russell-wilson">
             Russell Wilson
            </a>
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            G John Moffitt
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Schneider and head coach Pete Carroll have found a way to build a team with an eye on economics as well as talent. They have traded out of the first round the last two years, and due to the trade that got them tight end Jimmy Graham in March, the Seahawks wont be selecting in the first round (barring another trade) on April 30.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-31 cf display-none " data-page="31">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>
              Prev
             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">

              <span class="br-light-grey">

              </span>
              <span class="paginators_page-count">

             </a>

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Tampa Bay Buccaneers: Jason Licht
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Tampa Bay Buccaneers: Jason Licht" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/443/hi-res-a7e1e32b33d7aa60e0f5dbe3680c5a48_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Phelan M. Ebenhack/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Jason Licht, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Tampa Bay Buccaneers
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            The well-traveled executive took over as the Buccaneers general manager just last year. His past front-office stints around the NFL include stops with the Miami Dolphins (where he began his pro career in 1995), Carolina Panthers, New England Patriots, Philadelphia Eagles and Arizona Cardinals.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            2-14
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            WR Mike Evans
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            Its just one draft with the Buccaneers, but it is interesting to note that Licht was a little light on defense. All six of Tampa Bays selections in 2014 came on the offensive side of the football. And from all indications, the team is about to make it seven straight picks on offense if they grab Florida State quarterback Jameis Winston with the No. 1 overall pick. Stay tuned.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-32 cf display-none " data-page="32">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Tennessee Titans: Ruston Webster
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Tennessee Titans: Ruston Webster" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/444/hi-res-5ec3166f99beab1286b7117420da4f0c_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Frederick Breedon/Getty Images
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Ruston Webster, Executive VP/General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Tennessee Titans
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            Webster begins his fourth season as Tennessees general manager, promoted by the team after being the clubs vice president of player personnel the previous two years. Prior to being hired by the Titans, he was the Seattle Seahawks vice president of player personnel from 2006-09. Before that, Webster spent 18 years with the Tampa Bay Buccaneers from 1988-2005.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            15-33
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits:
            </strong>
            DT Jurrell Casey
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses:
            </strong>
            No big misses yet
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            In each of the last two drafts, Webster has opted to bolster his offensive line
            <span>
             in the first round
            </span>
            with the addition of guard Chance Warmack and tackle Taylor Lewan, respectively. Back in 2012, he selected wide receiver Kendall Wright with the 20th overall pick. Dont be shocked if the Titans opt for some much-needed defensive help with the second overall selection on April 30.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
         <section class="article_page article_page--secondary js-article-page-33 cf display-none " data-page="33">
          <header class="article_page-header">
           <div class="article_nav-bar br-texture--sudo br-texture--sudo-fade-to-white">
            <div class="paginators paginators--top">
             <a class="paginator paginator--secondary paginator--prev" href="javascript: void(0)" title="Previous Page">
              <span class="aquo">
               
              </span>

             </a>
             <div class="paginators_counter">

              <span class="br-light-grey">

            <h2 class="article_page-title" itemprop="alternativeHeadline">
             Washington Redskins: Scot McCloughan
            </h2>
           </div>
          </header>
          <div class="article_image" itemprop="associatedMedia">
           <div class="article_image--main " itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" style="max-width:630px">
            <img alt="Washington Redskins: Scot McCloughan" data-defer-src="http://img.bleacherreport.net/img/slides/photos/003/925/450/hi-res-51ef9aa9820c70a3d5413142adc87093_crop_north.jpg?w=630&amp;h=420&amp;q=75" height="420" itemprop="contentURL" src="data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAAAEAAAABCAQAAAC1HAwCAAAAC0lEQVQIHWNgYAAAAAMAAU9ICq8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=" width="630"/>
            <div class="caption-overlay border-box" max-width="630">
            </div>
            <div class="article_image-accreditation" max-width="630">
             <span>
              Nick Wass/Associated Press
             </span>
             <br/>
            </div>
           </div>
          </div>
          <div class="article_body cf" itemprop="articleBody">
           <p>
            <strong>
             Name/Title:
            </strong>
            Scot McCloughan, General Manager
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team:
            </strong>
            Washington Redskins
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Background:
            </strong>
            He has certainly made his mark around the NFL since 2000. McCloughan enjoyed two stints with the Seattle Seahawks in different capacities, but his most noted accomplishments came during his days with the San Francisco 49ers, where he was the teams vice president of football operations and later the clubs general manager for a combined five years from 2005-09. McCloughans work with the Niners is reflected in the listed hits and misses.
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Team Record as GM:
            </strong>
            First season with Redskins
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Hits (with 49ers):
            </strong>
            RB Frank Gore, TE
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/vernon-davis">
             Vernon Davis
            </a>
            , LB
            <a href="http://bleacherreport.com/patrick-willis">
             Patrick Willis
            </a>
            , T Joe Staley
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Biggest Draft Misses (with 49ers):
            </strong>
            WR Jason Hill, DT Kentwan Balmer
           </p>
           <p>
            <strong>
             Draft Trends:
            </strong>
            For the first time since 2012, the Redskins have a first-round draft choice. Of course, thats hardly a shocker for a franchise that has chosen only 25 players in the first round in the 48-year history of the common draft. Meanwhile, McCloughan had a pair of first-round picks when he was with the 49ers in both 2006 and 2007.
           </p>
          </div>
         </section>
        </div>

        // If we've already installed the SDK, we're done
        if (document.getElementById('facebook-jssdk')) {return;}

        // Get the first script element, which we'll use to find the parent node
